If Youre a Woman, You're Increasing Your Cancer Risk.","summary":"Youve heard it repeatedly: Sitting is the new smoking. But while experts agree we could all stand to get off our butts a little more, new research on the topic has a startling discovery.","body":"\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F1123feef6683ed83c057ac32b81bb079702be45a.gif\" alt=\"Sitting Down for This? If You&#x2019;re a Woman, You&apos;re Increasing Your Cancer Risk.\" width=\"540\" height=\"360\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cb\u003EWomen may have estrogen to thank, researchers say. \u003C\u002Fb\u003E(Photo: Getty Images)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EYou&#x2019;ve heard it repeatedly: Sitting is the new smoking. But while experts agree we could all stand to get off our butts a little more, new research on the topic has a startling discovery: Women have a higher risk of developing cancer from sitting.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EA study of 146,000 men and women published in the journal Cancer Epidemiology, Biomarkers &amp; Prevention discovered that women who spend moreof their downtime sitting are at a 10 percent higher risk of developing cancer, specifically multiple myeloma, breast, and ovarian cancers.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EMen, on the other hand, had no increased risk of developing cancer after sitting.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EStudy author Alpha Patel, PhD, strategic director at the American Cancer Society,tells Yahoo Health that she wasn&#x2019;t shocked by her research&#x2019;s finding that sitting may cause cancer since &#x201C;there is a growing body of scientific evidence to suggest that sitting time may be associated with cancer and other disease risk.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EHowever, she&#x2019;s a little stumped on why there&#x2019;s a gender difference. Patel says it could be because she only studied how much people sat during their leisure time(i.e. not at work), or there may be a true biological reason.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EThis isn&#x2019;t the first research that found women may be more at risk for developing cancer from sitting.\u003C\u002Fb\u003E&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe American Cancer Society&#x2019;s Cancer Prevention Study II discovered that women who sat for six or more hours a day had a 37 percent greater risk of death compared to those who sat for three hours or less a day. Butmen only had a 17 percent greater risk.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Ci\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002Fthe-two-minute-solution-to-sitting-all-day-117699178657.html\"\u003EThe Two-Minute Solution to Sitting All Day\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe disparity was even greater for those who didn&#x2019;t exercise: Women who were inactive and sat for long periods of time were at a 94 percent higher risk of developing cancer, while men were at a 48 percent higher risk.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EWhat&#x2019;s going on here?\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIt may all be due to estrogen, says medical oncologist Homayoon Sanati, MD, medical director of the MemorialCare Breast Center at Orange Coast Memorial Medical Center in Fountain Valley, Calif.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EHe explains it this way to Yahoo Health: Ovarian and breast cancers are related to an increase in the production of estrogen. Sitting can increase the production of estrogen in a woman&#x2019;s body through the development of extra fat cells that happen when a woman has a sedentary lifestyle.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EEstrogen promotes the growth of breast and ovarian cells and, when more cells grow, there is an increased risk that those cells can have genomic errors that may lead to the development of cancer.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EHowever, Sanati says men probably can&#x2019;t become couch potatoes without consequences. &#x201C;The study only looked at cancers diagnosed between 1992 and 2009,&#x201D; he points out. &#x201C;For men, prostate cancer may be diagnosed at the later stages of life.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EResearch has repeatedly found a link between sitting and negative health consequences &#x2014; for women and men.\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAn analysis of 47 studies published in the journal Annals of Internal Medicine in January found that people who sat for long periods of time were 24 percent more likely to die from health problems within 16 years.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBut working out might not help: A 2010 study published in the journal Exercise and Sport Sciences Reviews discovered that physical activity alone may not be enough to off-set the negative health risks of sitting. And a 2011 study published in the journal Metabolism found that the body&#x2019;s insulin response goes down after just one day of sitting, which can lead to the development of diabetes and other diseases.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Ci\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002Fsitting-with-your-legs-crossed-4-reasons-to-stop-113359313402.html\"\u003ESitting With Your Legs Crossed? 4 Reasons To Stop\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EPatel says that researchers still aren&#x2019;t sure how much sitting is safe. &#x201C;The evidence to date supports that sitting less (compared to more) is associated with lower risk of some types of cancer, cardiovascular disease, diabetes, and premature death from any cause,&#x201D; she says. &#x201C;However, the exact amount that is considered safe is still being studied.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBut Sanati says more movement seems to be better: &#x201C;We know, for example, &#xA0;that for women who have already had breast cancer, those who are involved in more physical activity have less of a chance of recurrence of the disease.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EHe tells his patients that some sitting is fine, but to do it in moderation. And, if you have to sit for a long period of time, get up and walk for a few minutes after a half hour before sitting down again &#x2014; it could save your life.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERead This Next: \u003Ci\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002Fsitting-down-for-too-long-may-increase-anxiety-121935808942.html\"\u003ESitting Down for Too Long May Increase Anxiety\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003ELet&#x2019;s keep in touch! WomenRegret Abortions? NewStudy Helps End Debate","summary":"We find that the negative emotions experienced at the time of the abortion wane\u002Fdecrease significantly over 3 years afterwards. Notably, relief remains the most common emotion.","body":"\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F17c659b4aa495afafaad534d874ca2c03e96c795.jpg\" width=\"540\" height=\"360\" alt=\"Do Women&#xA0;&#x2018;Regret&#x2019; Abortions? New&#xA0;Study Helps End Debate\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cb\u003E&#x201C;We find that the negative emotions experienced at the time of the abortion wane\u002Fdecrease significantly over 3 years afterwards. Notably, relief remains the most common emotion.&#x201D; \u003C\u002Fb\u003E(Photo: Getty Images)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ENew research has found that \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fjournals.plos.org\u002Fplosone\u002Farticle?id=10.1371\u002Fjournal.pone.0128832\"\u003Emore than 95 percent of women\u003C\u002Fa\u003E who have received an abortion have no regret about it, feeling that their decision was the right thing for them. Researchers found no difference in mental health outcomes between women who had first-trimester abortions and late-term abortions.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.guttmacher.org\u002Fstatecenter\u002Fspibs\u002Fspib_MWPA.pdf\"\u003EThirty-five states\u003C\u002Fa\u003E currently require some for of \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.guttmacher.org\u002Fpubs\u002Fgpr\u002F10\u002F4\u002Fgpr100406.html\"\u003Emandatory counseling\u003C\u002Fa\u003E for a woman before an abortion can be performed, \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.guttmacher.org\u002Fstatecenter\u002Fspibs\u002Fspib_MWPA.pdf\"\u003Eseven\u003C\u002Fa\u003E of which require a woman be told of possible psychological responses to abortion, stressing negative emotional responses such as &#x201C;\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.psychologytoday.com\u002Fblog\u002Fsomatic-psychology\u002F201010\u002Fpost-abortion-stress-syndrome-pass-does-it-exist\"\u003Epostabortion traumatic stress disorder\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&#x201D;, a term adopted by pro-life supporters but has not been accepted by the American Psychological Association or the American Psychiatric Association, and is basically debunked by this study.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe study, commissioned by \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.ansirh.org\u002F\"\u003EAdvancing New Standards in Reproductive Health (ANSIRH)\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, a think-tank at the University of California, San Francisco, confirms thirty years of research explicitly pointing towards there being no adverse mental health effects from abortion.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;As we note in our 2013 paper on women&#x2019;s emotions one week after the abortion, we found that many women experience negative emotions (anger, sadness, guilt, regret), as well as positive emotions (relief, happiness), with relief predominating,&#x201D; \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fbixbycenter.ucsf.edu\u002Ffs\u002Fbios\u002Frocca-corinne.html\"\u003ECorinne Rocca\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, PhD, MPH, an epidemiologist at the University of California-San Francisco and part of the ANSIRH research team, tells Yahoo Health, noting that in the team&#x2019;s new research, &#x201C;we find that the negative emotions experienced at the time of the abortion wane\u002Fdecrease significantly over 3 years afterwards. Notably, relief remains the most common emotion.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIn 2011, the Academy of Medical Royal Colleges (AMRC) in London reviewed all studies about the emotional effects of abortion that had been published in English between 1990 and 2011; from this, they concluded that it is an unwanted pregnancy that increases a woman&#x2019;s risk of problems with her mental health. AMRC researchers also deduced that a woman with an unwanted pregnancy is as likely to have mental health problems from abortion as she is from giving birth.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Ci\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002Fi-set-her-free-what-one-woman-wants-lawmakers-118896673772.html\"\u003EWhat One Woman Wants Lawmakers to Know About Her Late-Term Abortion&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe AMRC team also found that the factors that do increase a woman&#x2019;s risk of mental health problems after abortion are pressure from a partner to terminate a pregnancy, negative attitudes about abortion, and negative attitudes about a woman&#x2019;s experience of abortion.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIn other words, the stigma around abortion is more dangerous to a woman&#x2019;s mental health than abortion itself.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe ANSIRH researchers came to a similar conclusion, finding that it was women who perceived abortion stigma in their community (as well as those who terminated a planned and wanted pregnancy after the discovery of fetal abnormalities) that experiences for negative emotions.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;There is definitely a perception in public discourse over abortion that later abortion is more emotionally difficult than abortion in the first trimester, which is when over 90 percent of abortions in the US are done,&#x201D; says Rocca. &#x201C;In fact, as we note in the paper, the possibility that women having later procedures might be more likely to regret their abortions was part of the Supreme Court&#x2019;s justification for upholding a 2007 law banning a later abortion procedure. Our findings do not support this conclusion at all. Instead, we found that the emotions felt by women having abortions near gestational limits and women having first-trimester procedures reported the same levels of emotions; both experienced declines in negative emotions over time; and &#x201C;decision rightness&#x201D; was high among both groups.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EMost dramatically, the ANSIRH team also found that the predicted probability that 99 percent of women will ultimately report that abortion was the right decision for them at all time points in a three-year span following having received an abortion. The researchers also reported that &#x201C;being in school and working at the time of the pregnancy was associated with far higher feelings of decision rightness.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003ERelated:\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002Fwomen-face-harder-path-to-abortion-as-states-118873862652.html\"\u003E Women Face Harder Path to Abortion as States Extend Waiting Period \u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe researchers also drew an important &#x2014; albeit nuanced &#x2014; conclusion about the often politicized conversation surrounding abortion and women&#x2019;s mental health, stating that, &#x201C;Certainly, experiencing feelings of guilt or regret in the short-term after an abortion is not a mental health problem; in fact, such emotions are a normal part of making a life decision that many women in this study found to be difficult.&#x201D; That is, it is critical to not misinterpret emotions that come with normal life experiences as being negative side effects of abortion. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E &#x201C;Abortion has become an increasingly politicized topic in the US,&#x201D; notes Rocca. &#x201C;Groups interested in making it harder for women to get abortions have used the mental health damage argument to forward legislation restricting access. I think part of the reason these arguments perpetuate and continue to shape public perception has been the lack of rigorously conducted research examining the topic&#x2026;.Our study was very unique in that we are following hundreds of women seeking abortions at 30 facilities across diverse parts of the US over years to prospectively assess emotional and mental health outcomes. And, our findings do not support claims that abortion causes harmful psychological problems.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERead This Next:&#xA0;\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002Fmedical-abortion-can-be-safer-and-easier-for-women-109298214527.html\"\u003EMedical Abortion Can Be Safer and Easier for Women &#x2014; So Why Follow Old Protocols?\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003ELet&#x2019;s keep in touch! of the Best Things You Can Do for Someone With a Severe Mental Illness","summary":"Having an episode of psychosis or mania is hard.","body":"\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002Fa45aae7fe1fefb3babca89d60e3d6262d28563c9.jpg\" alt=\"One of the Best Things You Can Do for Someone With a Severe Mental Illness\" width=\"540\" height=\"357\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EHaving an episode of psychosis or mania is hard. Trying to put the pieces of my life back together afterward is brutal. But the things society says to me every day chip away pieces of myself, even when I should be repairing the damage.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EOnce a psychotic episode is over and I can think rationally, the things I did and said while psychotic cause me great shame. Not only do I have to live with telling people I was Jesus, how the government was out to get me, that I was being filmed or recorded or any number of other delusions I may have during an episode, I also have to live with the day to day barrage of messages from the outside &#x2014; messages that tell me I&#x2019;m dangerous and that my illness is something to make light of, even make fun of. I have to live with that stigma.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated:\u003C\u002Fb\u003E \u003Cb\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fthemighty.com\u002F2014\u002F09\u002Fwhen-i-noticed-my-wife-crying-behind-her-sunglasses\u002F?utm_source=yahoo.com&amp;utm_medium=referral&amp;utm_campaign=yahoo_links&amp;utm_content=Wife_Crying_Behind_Sunglasses\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003EWhen I Noticed My Wife Crying Behind Her Sunglasses\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EI&#x2019;m not going to go into all of the jokes and memes people say on social media every day that chip away at my self-esteem, but I will say that even people who like to call themselves progressive, loving and accepting join in the &#x201C;fun.&#x201D; Even people who think they are sensitive to social situations and people who are marginalized toss out words like insane, nut-job, lunatic and pass around cartoons depicting a &#x201C;crazy&#x201D; lady with PMS.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EWhen I see those words written from people who claim to like or love me, all I feel from them is a lack of understanding and hate. Yes, I literally feel as if they are sending hate at those who live with mental illness, and at me. Everyone in my life knows that I have schizophrenia. Anyone that wants to know what schizophrenia is like can read my book, Pills, Poetry &amp; Prose: Life with Schizophrenia, read my blog or even more amazing, they can ask me.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated:\u003C\u002Fb\u003E \u003Cb\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fthemighty.com\u002F2015\u002F02\u002Fi-have-ocd-this-is-what-its-like-to-be-in-my-mind-for-3-minutes2?utm_source=yahoo.com&amp;utm_medium=referral&amp;utm_campaign=yahoo_links&amp;utm_content=I_Have_OCD\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003EI Have OCD. This Is What It&#x2019;s Like to Be in My Mind for 3 Minutes.\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIf someone were to ask me what having schizophrenia is like, I would tell them it can be like going to a place with your worst fears, and living those fears out for days, weeks and possibly months. Are you afraid of being tortured? You will believe you are about to be tortured. Are you afraid of going to jail? You will believe you are going to jail. And then sometimes during psychosis, you will even be afraid of things you didn&#x2019;t know you were afraid of. I can think of nothing more appropriate to call it than hell on earth. In the beginning psychosis is usually pleasant for me, but it always turns to terror over time, and that terror is total and complete.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ESo, if you ever wonder what you can do for someone with a severe mental illness, I have a suggestion: You can help build them up. The world is already constantly tossing self-esteem battering messages their way. You can be the change in their lives. You can help them see their talents. You can help them see their strengths. You can point out their positives. You can be kind to them, because it is tough. It is so damn tough, and we all get tired. It&#x2019;s exhausting to constantly tell yourself you&#x2019;re OK when the world says differently. It&#x2019;s almost impossible to fight the world on your own. Be an ally. Spread the love.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated:\u003C\u002Fb\u003E \u003Cb\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fthemighty.com\u002F2015\u002F05\u002F31-secrets-of-people-who-live-with-anxiety\u002F?utm_source=yahoo.com&amp;utm_medium=referral&amp;utm_campaign=yahoo_links&amp;utm_content=Secrets_Anxiety\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003E31 Secrets of People Who Live With Anxiety\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003Eby \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fthemighty.com\u002Fauthor\u002Frebecca-chamaa\u002F\"\u003ERebecca Chamaa\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EMore from The Mighty:\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fthemighty.com\u002F2014\u002F10\u002Fwhen-i-overheard-a-conversation-between-my-son-with-autism-and-his-brother?utm_source=yahoo.com&amp;utm_medium=referral&amp;utm_campaign=yahoo_links&amp;utm_content=Conversation_Between_Brothers\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003EWhen I Overheard a Conversation Between My Son With Autism and His Brother\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fthemighty.com\u002F2015\u002F03\u002Fi-let-my-4-year-old-with-autism-use-my-camera-heres-how-he-sees-the-world\u002F?utm_source=yahoo.com&amp;utm_medium=referral&amp;utm_campaign=yahoo_links&amp;utm_content=Autism_Camera\"\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003EI Let My 4-Year-Old With Autism Use My Camera. Here&#x2019;s How He Sees the World.\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca \u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EI&#x2019;m talking firm-fleshed, flavorful, meaty ones like halibut and salmon that can handle heat, the smoke, and a flip or two. To prep a grill for hardy fish, start by cranking it as high as it will go. You want the grates very, very hot, so cover the grill as it heats up. &#xA0;Once the grill is hot, use a steel brush with a long handle and some elbow grease to completely clean the grates. &#xA0;Cover again for 2 to 3 more minutes to bring the grates back to that piping hot level. &#xA0;(If using a grill pan on the stove, follow the same process; just make sure the exhaust fan is on high and a window is open.)\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated:\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Ffood52.com\u002Fblog\u002F10975-two-ways-to-perfect-a-fish-glaze?utm_source=yahoohealth&amp;utm_medium=referral&amp;utm_campaign=fiveminutefish\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003E 2 ways to perfect a fish glaze\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"359\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F40d6a32577526e99ecec0f333ff0947dcd648b51.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E(Photo: thirschfeld)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EEach fish steak you are planning to cook should weight about six ounces, be at least a solid inch thick, and kept very cold.\u003C\u002Fb\u003E Remove the steaks from the refrigerator just before you are ready to grill and pat them dry.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated:\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Ffood52.com\u002Fblog\u002F13360-grilling-crab-is-easier-than-you-think?utm_source=yahoohealth&amp;utm_medium=referral&amp;utm_campaign=fiveminutefish\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003E Grilling crab is easier than you think\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EDampen a wad of paper towels with canola or grapeseed oil liberally. Grab the oiled towels with a pair of tongs, and rub them along the grates of the grill. Reduce the heat to medium high and place the fish on the grill, skin-side up (there may be no skin on your fish steaks, but I am referring to the side that used to have the skin on).\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Ffood52.com\u002Fblog\u002F13258-what-to-do-with-leftover-salmon?utm_source=yahoohealth&amp;utm_medium=referral&amp;utm_campaign=fiveminutefish\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003EWhat to do with leftover salmon\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAfter about 2 minutes, the lower half of the fish steak closest to the heat will start to turn opaque. That&#x2019;s when you know it&#x2019;s time to flip. Use a spatula (one that is wide and has a tapered edge) to gently loosen the underside of the fish steak from the grill and flip quickly. Cook for another 2 to 4 minutes, depending on the thickness of the fish. To test if the steak is done, gently use a spatula to pry open the middle contours of the fish. If they are opaque, you&#x2019;re good to go. &#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Ffood52.com\u002Fblog\u002F13257-escabeche-the-best-make-ahead-post-beach-dinner?utm_source=yahoohealth&amp;utm_medium=referral&amp;utm_campaign=fiveminutefish\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003EEscabeche: the best make-ahead post-beach dinner\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ETo serve, pair your grilled fish with one of the following simple sauces:\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"360\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F09e2bcbb10e6cd7f17406533a203112ec60e91de.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E(Photo: Alpha Smoot)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EI have my biases, of course.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cul\u003E\n \u003Cli\u003ELoosen Em-i-lis&#x2019;s Mint-Pistachio Pesto with just a bit more olive oil than the recipe calls for, and it will make a piece of grilled halibut seem Mediterranean even though it doesn&#x2019;t swim there.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n \u003Cli\u003EThe ingredients in hardlikearmor&#x2019;s Green Harissa make a versatile topping.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n \u003Cli\u003EGenius Recipes Torrisi&#x2019;s Spicy Sauce stands up to a fish with strong flavor.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg A new study has found that probiotic-laced foods like yogurt can balance out your gut bacteria in a way that significantly improves the way you feel about your life. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThink of your gut bacteria as your own internal spin doctors, dictating whether your mood is going to be positive, or downbeat. Recent research&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov\u002Fpubmed\u002F?term=steenbergen++probiotics+leiden\"\u003Epublished\u003C\u002Fa\u003E in the journal \u003Ci\u003EBrain, Behavior, and Immunity\u003C\u002Fi\u003E, researchers at Leiden University in The Netherlands recruited 40 healthy volunteers. Half of them were given a probiotic-laced supplement, the others a placebo. Over the next several months, they were asked about their feelings and their outlook on life. Within about four weeks, the group that was receiving the probiotics began to answer their surveys in ways that demonstrated fewer negative feelings and more positive ones! \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe key to this mood boost: Feeding your belly bugs with the right kind of yogurts&#x2014;those containing live, active cultures and not too much sugar (which promotes the growth of downer bugs). The editors of \u003Ci\u003EEat This, Not That! \u003C\u002Fi\u003Emagazine have identified some of the most effective mood boosters in the grocery store.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"501\" height=\"367\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w501\u002F78c851792a7996579cce03f85a4b5804e66a296a.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EBEST GREEK\u003Cbr\u003EFage Total 2% Greek Yogurt\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003EThere&#x2019;s a reason Fage is one of the most popular Greek yogurts out there. &#x201C;While it&#x2019;s not organic, Fage is one of the&#x2013;if not the&#x2013;best-tasting Greek yogurt available,&#x201D; says says Stephanie Middleberg, MS, RD, CDN. The brand is also impressively high in protein, packing in 20 grams per 7-ounce container, as much as any nutrition bar. Just make sure you side-step flavors like honey, which can pack a Snicker&#x2019;s bar worth of sugar.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"512\" height=\"375\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w512\u002F63433c9e4f33b14bc4f9b5751342431e8282fa40.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EBEST ORGANIC \u003Cbr\u003EStonyfield Organic Nonfat Greek Yogurt&#x2014;Plain\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003EBecause they are made with organic cow&#x2019;s milk, a container of Stonyfield Organic provides \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.plosone.org\u002Farticle\u002FAuthors\u002Finfo:doi\u002F10.1371\u002Fjournal.pone.0082429\"\u003Emore\u003C\u002Fa\u003E heart-healthy fatty acids than conventional yogurts. We suggest sticking with the plain variety on a daily basis, since it&#x2019;s low in sugar and calories, but if you&#x2019;re looking for a sweet morning treat, pick up their blueberry flavor. Though the sweet stuff slightly outweighs the protein, it&#x2019;s a perfectly acceptable once-in-a-while, probiotic-filled treat. For more tricks to reduce bloat, improve mood&#x2014;and uncover your abs&#x2014;tap for these \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.zerobelly.com\u002F14-ways-to-lose-your-belly-in-14-days\"\u003E14 Ways to Lose Your Belly in 14 Days\u003C\u002Fa\u003E!\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"456\" height=\"334\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w456\u002F0d59298f616a12b949a3e5b0a0d5efcb7ed7ff8f.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EBEST GRASS-FED\u003Cbr\u003EMaple Hill Creamery Greek Yogurt\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003EMaple Hill Creamery&#x2019;s yogurts are made just two ingredients: grass-fed milk and live cultures&#x2014;and although you pay a premium for it, it&#x2019;s worth the few extra cents. &#x201C;Grass-fed yogurt contains more omega-3s and conjugated linoleic acids, both of which help prevent heart disease, inflammation, diabetes and various cancers,&#x201D; Middleberg says. Bonus: The blends are rich, creamy and taste fresh from the farm.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"512\" height=\"300\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w512\u002F8deb885444e9d7a1fdf38cb0140092148736c726.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EBEST ALT-YOGURT\u003Cbr\u003EElli Quark \u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003EGerman for &#x201C;fresh curd,&#x201D; quark is a spoonable cheese that&#x2019;s a creamier version of your go-to yogurt&#x2014;and could be the next big thing in the daily aisle. To achieve the thick, indulgent texture, makers stir curd to stop it from hardening, and the result is a smooth dairy cream that&#x2019;s free of the tang typically associated with unflavored Greek yogurts. The relatively neutral flavor lends itself well to adding your favorite mix-ins. Plus, just like Greek yogurt, quark is filled with good-for-you probiotics and hunger-busting protein. (There&#x2019;s up to 17 grams in a 6-ounce container.) They both have about the same number of calories, too. These additional cultures have been \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.andjrnl.org\u002Farticle\u002FS0002-8223(03)00207-4\u002Fabstract\"\u003Eshown\u003C\u002Fa\u003E to improve lactose digestion, reducing bloating and gas in sensitive individuals by 70 percent. Each cup of Lifeway&#x2019;s Veggie Kefir delivers 9 grams of protein and just 12 grams of sugar, for only 100 calories. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"512\" height=\"376\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w512\u002Fe062041e676b9fc2cf912ebc0bb528e74842c5e7.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EBEST SWEET YOGURT\u003Cbr\u003EChobani Simply 100 Vanilla\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003EWith just 100 calories, 7 grams of sugar and nearly double that amount of protein, this just-sweet-enough yogurt is a waist-friendly pick&#x2014;something most other flavored containers can&#x2019;t claim. For an added boost of antioxidants, top it off with some fresh berries, or if you prefer more crunch, mix in a few spoonfuls of whole-grain cereal. Brain Chemistry Behind Just One Bite And How To Beat It","summary":"You and dark chocolate have a long-standing love affair.","body":"\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F805ee198a6b7429fd12eedd1094aa251823b27d2.jpg\" alt=\"The Brain Chemistry Behind &#x201C;Just One Bite&#x201D; And How To Beat It\" width=\"540\" height=\"306\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EYou and \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.charlottesbook.com\u002Ffavorite-healthy-chocolate-bars\u002F\"\u003Edark chocolate\u003C\u002Fa\u003E have a long-standing love affair. You&#x2019;re seduced every night. You&#x2019;d like to be monogamous, but coconut ice cream calls you. So do vegan chocolate chip cookies and crusty bread with olive oil. Cognitively, you know you shouldn&#x2019;t be eating these foods, but once you&#x2019;ve had a bite, you&#x2019;re done. You&#x2019;re intoxicated.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.psychologytoday.com\u002Fbasics\u002Fdopamine\"\u003EDopamine\u003C\u002Fa\u003E floods the brain and you continue eating these foods until there&#x2019;s nothing left. Moderation doesn&#x2019;t exist in your world, even though you wish it did. You really wish it did. You want nothing more than to be in control of what you put into your mouth. Why does it feel like there&#x2019;s an invisible hand guiding you towards these temptations? Why does it always feel like you need&#xA0;\u003Ci\u003Eone more bite? \u003C\u002Fi\u003EWe did a little investigating here at \u003Cb\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.charlottesbook.com\"\u003ECharlotte&#x2019;s Book\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E and asked Food Coach NYC, \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.charlottesbook.com\u002Fauthor\u002Fdana_james\u002F\"\u003EDana James\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EIt&#x2019;s All In The Chemistry (So Relax About Your Willpower)\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe answer lies in your brain chemistry: neurotransmitters and conditioning. It&#x2019;s not your willpower, so drop the self-flagellation. Instead, be aware that there are biochemical forces at play. The good news is that you have the power to transcend these.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EYou&#x2019;re not driven in search of a dopamine high like a strung-out junkie, nor are you one of Pavlov&#x2019;s dogs, conditioned to salivate at the ring of a bell. You&#x2019;re a human being with the ability to stop, observe and change behavior at any moment. Being aware of what you&#x2019;re up against is the first part of breaking the addiction.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EThe Feel-Good Signal\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EWhen you eat a sweet food, it immediately sends a signal to the brain to release dopamine, a pleasure neurotransmitter. Dopamine feels good. It gives a sense of relief. It&#x2019;s the same neurotransmitter that is released during sex, recreational drug use and flirtation. Who doesn&#x2019;t want a little dopamine hit? Unfortunately, the more you provoke dopamine with food, sex, or drugs, the more your body stops listening to it. The result: you need even more stimuli for the same high. More chocolate, more ice cream, and more bread. If you think dark chocolate and bread don&#x2019;t have sugar, you&#x2019;ve been tricked. One quarter of a 70% dark chocolate bar is sugar, and bread converts to sugar.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated :&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.charlottesbook.com\u002Fcharlottes-pages\u002Fmenu-luminous-skin\u002F\"\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003EMaximize Your Menu For Glowing, Luminous Skin\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThere&#x2019;s also a serotonin influence and an endorphin response, particularly if the food contains wheat or dairy. Eat both dairy and wheat together and you&#x2019;ll hijack your brain with so many stimuli&#xA0;you may as well be injecting yourself with Prozac and Wellbutrin, because that&#x2019;s exactly what they do&#x2014;recycle old serotonin and dopamine so you have more.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERe-Train Your Brain, Defeat Your Subconscious Reactions\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ENinety-five percent of our actions are based on our subconscious. Our subconscious is defined by memorized behaviors, emotional reactions, attitudes and beliefs. If you&#x2019;ve trained your body to over-eat, binge or numb yourself with food, that&#x2019;s what it&#x2019;s going to do, even if 5% of the brain is telling it not to. This is why it feels like there&#x2019;s an invisible force driving you towards something you know you shouldn&#x2019;t be doing. This pattern can be broken.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated:&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.charlottesbook.com\u002Fcharlottes-pages\u002Freduce-bloat-fodmap-defined\u002F\"\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003EA Recipe to Reduce Bloat, Not Weight: FODMAP Defined\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAbstain from your trigger foods for 21 days so you can rebalance your brain chemistry. If this sends fear running through your body, you&#x2019;re using food as a drug. Food should produce a neutral response in the body. Therefore, it&#x2019;s even more imperative that you abstain. If you get a little teary, you&#x2019;re using food to numb an emotion. It&#x2019;s OK; we all do it. But that emotion enslaves you and binds you to food. Use pen and paper to get out how you feel. Food isn&#x2019;t there to medicate. It&#x2019;s there to heal.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cb\u003ENew Neural Pathways = New Habits\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EMake a different choice from the day before. Repeat, and repeat, and repeat, until the new behavior has become ingrained into your subconscious (typically 21 days). Don&#x2019;t underestimate how challenging this will be. You&#x2019;ll hear voices that will tell you it&#x2019;s OK to have just one bite, that you&#x2019;ve had a tough day and that you deserve it. The brain does this because it has to create new brain cells and new neural pathways to create a new habit. This is work for the body, and it doesn&#x2019;t like it.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBut you&#x2019;re not a slave to your brain. You&#x2019;re in control and you can direct it.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EWhat will your new habit be? What&#x2019;s going to keep you strong through the next 21 days?&#xA0;How will you feel when you break the addiction?\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ECommit to this now. Be free. Products May Be Contaminated With Salmonella\" width=\"540\" height=\"445\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cb\u003EThe recall comes after the USDA received reports that a cluster of people in Minnesota and Wisconsin became sick between mid-April and late June after eating Barber products.\u003C\u002Fb\u003E (Photo: Barber Foods)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBarber Foods is recalling more than 1.7 million pounds of frozen, raw, stuffed chicken that may be contaminated with salmonella, according to a \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.fsis.usda.gov\u002Fwps\u002Fportal\u002Ffsis\u002Ftopics\u002Frecalls-and-public-health-alerts\u002Frecall-case-archi\"\u003EU.S. Department of Agriculture&#x2019;s Food Safety and Inspection Services announcement\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe recall comes after the USDA received reports of people in Minnesota and Wisconsin who became sick between mid-April and late June after eating Barber products. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ENearly 30 products are included in the recall, which may be labeled under the brands Barber Foods, Sysco, or Meijer. (A full list of the products, along with their case code \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.fsis.usda.gov\u002Fwps\u002Fpor\"\u003Ecan be found here\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.)\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThis news comes after an original recall on July 2, in which the brand recalled more than 58,000 pounds of frozen, raw, stuffed chicken. The product in question was Barber Foods Premium Entrees Breaded-Boneless Raw Stuffed Chicken Breasts with Rib Meat Kiev with a use by\u002Fsell by date of April 28, 2016, May 20, 2016 and July 21, 2016.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ETwo additional patients have been identified by the USDA since the original recall, prompting the new announcement.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe particular strain of salmonella that has infected people&#x2014;salmonella enteritidis&#x2014;can cause fever, abdominal cramps, and diarrhea that begins 12 to 72 hours after a person eats contaminated food, according to the \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.cdc.gov\u002Fnczved\u002Fdivisions\u002Fdfbmd\u002Fdiseases\u002Fsalmonella_enteritidis\u002F\"\u003ECenters for Disease Control and Prevention\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. It usually lasts four to seven days, and can make a person sick enough to require hospitalization. Elderly people, children, and those who are immune-compromised are especially at risk.\u003C\u002Fp\u003EFood safety specialist Benjamin Chapman, PhD, an associate professor at North Carolina State University who has studied how people handle raw, frozen, stuffed, breaded chicken products, tells Yahoo Health that they&#x2019;re especially risky when it comes to salmonella.&#xA0;\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EWhy? Because of the way they appear, people assume that they&#x2019;re already cooked&#x2014;and don&#x2019;t cook them fully as a result. &#x201C;We have a responsibility to tell people that they need to cook these products properly,&#x201D; he says. &#x201C;I don&#x2019;t think we do a good job of it.&#x201D;\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Cbr\u003EHis research discovered that, despite properly labeling, only a small percentage of people actually use a thermometer to make sure their chicken is properly cooked, as recommended. Consequently, they&#x2019;re at risk of contracting salmonella from their meat. \u003Cbr\u003E\u003Cbr\u003EUnfortunately, freezing doesn&#x2019;t kill salmonella. The pathogen won&#x2019;t multiply when it&#x2019;s frozen, but will be preserved. So, when you take a frozen chicken product out of the freezer, it can still be contaminated.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Cbr\u003EFood safety expert Mike Doyle, PhD, director of the Center for Food Safety at the University of Georgia, says that proper cooking (bringing the meat&#x2019;s temperature to 165 degrees) will kill off the salmonella, but the real risk is in cross-contamination.&#x201C;\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Cbr\u003EIf you thaw the chicken, the juices can contain salmonella,&#x201D; he tells Yahoo Health. &#x201C;And if you thaw the chicken on a plate, cook it, and put the chicken on the same plate, it&#x2019;s been contaminated.&#x201D; Doyle also notes that you can get salmonella on your hands after handling the chicken, which can then be transferred to anything you touch.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003EThe USDA reports that some people who became sick had properly cooked the chicken and used a food thermometer to confirm that it was properly cooked. That&#x2019;s a sign that cross-contamination was an issue, says Doyle.\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe USDA stresses that while the products seem to be cooked, they&#x2019;re actually raw and should be handled with care to avoid cross-contamination in the kitchen. That means washing your hands and any surfaces after handling them, and keeping the chicken away from other food that won&#x2019;t be cooked.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003EIf you have any of these products in your freezer, it&#x2019;s safest to just throw them out. &#x201C;I wouldn&#x2019;t handle it,&#x201D; says Chapman. &#x201C;Send it back, take it to the seller, or get rid of them.&#x201D;&#xA0;\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe organization also reports some people who became sick had properly cooked the chicken and used a food thermometer to confirm that it was properly cooked. So, if you have any of these products in your freezer, it&#x2019;s probably safest to just throw them Women More Susceptible To Secondhand Smoke Exposure Than Men?","summary":"New research published in the American Journal of Preventative Medicine has found a consistent link between secondhand smoke and the risk of stroke. Interestingly, women are more at risk.","body":"\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002Fce216ce175dbf209e72d84ec34555b2f5c487a6d.jpg\" alt=\"Are Women More Susceptible To Secondhand Smoke Exposure Than Men?\" width=\"540\" height=\"365\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cb\u003EWhen you breathe secondhand smoke, it&#x2019;s &#x201C;like you are smoking,&#x201D; according to &#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.surgeongeneral.gov\u002Flibrary\u002Freports\u002F50-years-of-progress\u002Fexec-summary.pdf\"\u003ESurgeon General\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.&#xA0;2.5 million people have died in the U.S. from secondhand smoke exposure since 1964.\u003C\u002Fb\u003E&#xA0;(Photo: Getty Images)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe dangers of secondhand smoke have been studied for years, and research concludes the same thing: it&#x2019;s definitely bad for you.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ENow, new research published in the American Journal of Preventative Medicine has found a consistent link between secondhand smoke and the risk of stroke. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe study, which analyzed data from more than 20,000 nonsmokers aged 45 and up, found that those who were exposed to secondhand smoke were 30 percent more likely to suffer a stroke within six years.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAnd, here&#x2019;s a noteworthy additional finding: Researchers discovered that study participants who were exposed to secondhand smoke were more likely to live with a smoker &#x2014; and be female.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EWhile the study&#x2019;s authors tell Yahoo Health the finding could simply be due to sampling, psychologists say they&#x2019;re not shocked.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ELicensed clinical psychologist \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Faliciaclarkpsyd.com\u002F\"\u003EAlicia Clark\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, PsyD, tells Yahoo Health that women can have difficulty speaking up when their needs are in conflict with those of someone they love, as is often the case when smokers and non-smokers live together. &#x201C;Women are nurturers by nature, and this tendency likely influences how women navigate conflict,&#x201D; she says. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Ci\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002Fare-former-smokers-safe-after-15-years-121685128937.html\"\u003EAre Former Smokers&#xA0;&#x201C;Safe&#x201D; After 15 Years?&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAs a result, she says, a woman may be more likely to avoid the inevitable conflict that can come with raising an objection to her partner&#x2019;s smoking habit.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAtlanta-based psychologist and relationship therapist \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.dccatlanta.com\u002F\"\u003EJared DeFife\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, PhD, agrees, adding that the study may reflect a gender difference in how men and women handle assertion, boundaries, and limit setting in their relationships. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EWhile DeFife tells Yahoo Health that it&#x2019;s important to set boundaries and ground rules in relationships &#x2014; especially when it comes to your own health &#x2014; he acknowledges that a partner&#x2019;s smoking habit can be a tricky problem to navigate: &#x201C;When you have a partner who smokes and you want them to stop, you can be in a real bind.&#x201D; \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBut it&#x2019;s worth speaking up. According to the 2014 \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.surgeongeneral.gov\u002Flibrary\u002Freports\u002F50-years-of-progress\u002Fexec-summary.pdf\"\u003ESurgeon General&#x2019;s Report\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, 2.5 million people have died in the U.S. from secondhand smoke exposure since 1964. The Surgeon General also notes that, when you breathe secondhand smoke, it&#x2019;s &#x201C;like you are smoking.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAll secondhand smoke isn&#x2019;t created equal, and the \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.cancer.org\u002Fcancer\u002Fcancercauses\u002Ftobaccocancer\u002Fsecondhand-smoke\"\u003EAmerican Cancer Society\u003C\u002Fa\u003E breaks it into two categories: sidestream smoke (smoke from the lit end of a cigarette, pipe, or cigar) and mainstream smoke (smoke exhaled by a smoker). Sidestream smoke has higher concentrations of carcinogens, is more toxic than mainstream smoke, and has smaller particles that can make their way into your lungs and cells more easily &#x2014; and people who live with a smoker are repeatedly exposed to both.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated:\u003Ci\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002Fis-this-the-best-way-to-get-smokers-to-quit-118954738327.html\"\u003E Is This the Best Way to Get Smokers to Quit?&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ESecondhand smoke exposure doesn&#x2019;t just raise a person&#x2019;s risk of stroke. A report published in the journal \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fcirc.ahajournals.org\u002Fcontent\u002F111\u002F20\u002F2684.full\"\u003ECirculation\u003C\u002Fa\u003Econcluded that the negative effects on the heart from exposure to secondhand smoke are nearly as bad as the effects on those who actually smoke.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EPeople exposed to secondhand smoke may also be at risk of developing cancer. According to the \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.cdc.gov\u002Ftobacco\u002Fdata_statistics\u002Ffact_sheets\u002Fsecondhand_smoke\u002Fgeneral_facts\u002F\"\u003ECenters for Disease Control and Prevention\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, secondhand smoke exposure caused more than 7,300 lung cancer deaths each year between 2005 and 2009 among adult non-smokers.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ESecondhand smoke is also linked to marital issues: DeFife points to research that has found a partner&#x2019;s smoking habit is a &#x201C;significant predictor&#x201D; of later divorce. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ELuckily, overall secondhand smoke exposure is on the decline. CDC data found that, during 2011 to 2012, only 25 percent of nonsmokers had measurable levels of the tobacco smoke biomarker cotinine in their blood, compared to 40 percent during 2007 to 2008.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EDeFife says secondhand smoke may also be becoming less of an issue for younger women: &#x201C;Younger adults today appear to be less tolerant of dating, living with, or eventually marrying a partner who smokes.&#x201D; Those who actually are in a relationship with a smoker are more likely to relegate them to a smoking area outside, protecting their own health in the process, he says.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBottom line: If you live with a smoker and are exposed to secondhand smoke, you need to speak up. Your health depends on it.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERead This Next: \u003Ci\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002Fyikes-new-study-shows-scary-effect-of-smoking-on-110748176917.html\"\u003EYIKES: New Study Shows Scary Effect Of Smoking On The Brain\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003ELet&#x2019;s keep in touch! 0\u002F910a1647aa359f8b09d4875df0c50b8d074f42a2.jpg","type":"image\u002Fjpeg","width":450,"height":300,"size_type":"450","formats":{}},{"url":"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002F910a1647aa359f8b09d4875df0c50b8d074f42a2.jpg","type":"image\u002Fjpeg","width":500,"height":333,"size_type":"500","formats":{}},{"url":"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F910a1647aa359f8b09d4875df0c50b8d074f42a2.jpg","type":"image\u002Fjpeg","width":540,"height":360,"size_type":"original","formats":{}}],"url":"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002Foriginal\u002FxJkYdqeVlDBd9hY11DWXYZWKmCc","source_url":"http:\u002F\u002Fmagazines.zenfs.com\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002Foriginal\u002FxJkYdqeVlDBd9hY11DWXYZWKmCc"}],"highlight_color":"#000000","data_version":"1","title":"Meet the 23-Year-Old Whose Body Is Turning into Stone","summary":"Chanel White, age 23, is living with a rare chronic disease that slowly hardens her skin and organs.","body":"\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E \n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F4938094f495f8b08a0653e10e6c0c6565e15da31.jpg\" alt=\"Meet the 23-Year-Old Whose Body Is Turning into Stone\" width=\"540\" height=\"718\"\u003E \n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cb\u003EChanel White, age 23, is living with a rare chronic disease that slowly hardens her skin and organs.\u003C\u002Fb\u003E&#xA0;(Photo courtesy Chanel White)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EI was diagnosed with systemic scleroderma right after I turned 20, just a couple weeks after my honeymoon, in October 2011. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EI had never heard of scleroderma before the doctor told me I had it. \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.hopkinsscleroderma.org\u002Fscleroderma\u002F\"\u003EScleroderma\u003C\u002Fa\u003E is an autoimmune disease where the body produces too much collagen. It&#x2019;s as if someone is pumping concrete into your body.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EIn systemic scleroderma, the collagen not only builds up in your skin and your vascular system, but also your connective tissue, the framework of the human body. If you didn&#x2019;t have connective tissue, you would be like Gumby and you&#x2019;d just fall apart. If you have too much, like me, you basically turn into a living statue.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThe disease is rare &#x2014; fewer than 500,000 Americans have it &#x2014; and there is no cure. You could live five months or you could live 20 years. But based on how fast I started showing symptoms, when I was diagnosed, I was told 10 years would be fortunate. That was three years ago.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EIn that time, I&#x2019;ve realized that something so extremely broken can still be so beautiful. I&#x2019;ve learned that there is joy in letting go of what you can&#x2019;t change, in letting go of what you believe your life was intended to be, and instead accepting and celebrating and revering all that it gives. I can&#x2019;t do any more that my body will let me do and I have to accept that. Once you do that, you can find the beauty in a body vandalized like this.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002F10-things-id-like-people-to-know-about-living-122951065778.html\"\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003E10 Things I&#x2019;d Like People to Know About Living With a Chronic Illness\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EA Day in My Life\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EIn the media, you see stories of people who are doing all of these amazing things when they are sick, and honestly for me and many others it&#x2019;s not that way. There are lot of naps, a lot of doctor&#x2019;s appointments, a lot of medication taking, a lot of being too sick to do anything. I think people aren&#x2019;t as interested in that; it&#x2019;s boring, but it&#x2019;s the reality. Illness is not a glamorous existence, and it&#x2019;s important for people to know that.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EWhen I get up in the morning, there&#x2019;s just a lot of pain. There&#x2019;s always a fresh wave of pain when I wake up. It&#x2019;s just a realization that, yep, this is your body, this is what you&#x2019;re living. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EMy day starts with a handful of pills, a bunch of liquid supplementation, and getting my tube feed started. I take 28 different medications a day, each multiple times a day. I am overproducing collagen in my digestive tract, and so essentially my esophagus, my stomach, and my bowels are stone. I can&#x2019;t swallow food, and my stomach doesn&#x2019;t empty. It&#x2019;s like trying to drop nutrients into a rock. Everything is paralyzed.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EI&#x2019;m hooked up to tube feeds for 14 to 15 hours a day. The nutrition runs through a pump into a port in my abdomen. My stomach can&#x2019;t handle too much at once, so it has to go into my stomach very, very slowly &#x2014; about two ounces every hour.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003ETypically, I have anywhere from one to three medical appointments a day. I have a port in my chest for chemotherapy infusions. I have iron infusions every five days. I can have up to 20 appointments a month. It&#x2019;s overwhelming. There&#x2019;s not a lot of time to yourself when you&#x2019;re sick.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003ELife isn&#x2019;t very glamorous. There&#x2019;s a lot of Netflix watching and napping and puking and feeling horrible. There&#x2019;s also lots of talking to friends on Facebook, and blogging when I feel well enough. I live in pajamas. I probably own more pajamas than I do clothes.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EOn social media, I will post pictures of me smiling and wearing makeup when I do get out of the house. I don&#x2019;t want people to misinterpret the illness. But I also want to capture the moments where I&#x2019;m enjoying myself, because they won&#x2019;t happen often. I think it&#x2019;s important to show that you can still enjoy life in a broken body, but it&#x2019;s also important to have people understand that this one picture of me smiling is not me, it&#x2019;s the face that I put on. Those are the rare occasions that I try to enjoy when I get them. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated:\u003C\u002Fb\u003E \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002F7-things-i-want-teens-diagnosed-with-a-chronic-119457175518.html\"\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003E7 Things I Want Teens Diagnosed with a Chronic Illness to Know\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EA Sudden, Shocking Diagnosis\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EI started having symptoms just before I was diagnosed. It was almost one of those overnight things where you look down and just stare, wondering &#x201C;what is happening to my body?&#x201D; \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EMy hands would turn this horrible shade of violet purple, and they would go completely numb. I never thought much of it; I just thought my hands were cold. But I wasn&#x2019;t cold &#x2014; this was happening in a 70-degree room. After a few weeks of that, I started losing hair, I was tired all the time, and the tips of my fingers were starting to look kind of weird.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EOne day, I looked down and I thought I had burnt my finger cooking. It looked like I had just sat my finger on a hot grill. It was black and scabby, and horrendously painful. Every time I touched it was excruciating. It didn&#x2019;t go away and wasn&#x2019;t getting better, so I finally went to a doctor. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EHe took one look at me and told me, &#x201C;You have scleroderma.&#x201D; \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003ETypically, a scleroderma diagnosis takes years. Many people are misdiagnosed with lupus or other autoimmune diseases. I walked in and literally didn&#x2019;t even have a chance to say hello before the doctor was like, &#x201C;You have this horrible disease.&#x201D; I didn&#x2019;t know what to do. He gave me pamphlets to read, tons of medication to pick up from the pharmacy, and a new way of life to start. I started chemotherapy pills and immune suppressants right away. Immediately after that appointment, it was a drastic life change.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EMy fingers are tight and swollen; I can&#x2019;t straighten them. They get these sores &#x2014; that word really doesn&#x2019;t do them justice &#x2014; they&#x2019;re ulcerations, dead skin and tissue. It&#x2019;s because that concrete is not only harming my skin, but it&#x2019;s also crushing my vascular system. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EA lot of people when I first received the diagnosis thought it only affected my hands. They&#x2019;d ask, &#x201C;How are your hands doing?&#x201D; And I kept trying to explain to them, &#x201C;Yes, you can see that my hands are purple, you can see they have sores on them, but that&#x2019;s also happening to my organs.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EBecoming My Own Casket\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003ESince my diagnosis, it has been a snowball of one problem after another. In December 2014, I was walking up the stairs to the mall and collapsed. I was wheeled out and rushed to the emergency room. My body had just stopped. I couldn&#x2019;t walk, I couldn&#x2019;t lift my head &#x2014; I was lying in a hospital bed with a machine breathing for me. I was basically awake for a month but couldn&#x2019;t do anything on my own.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EI don&#x2019;t have much of an immune system, so I get sick very easily. I ended up with meningitis, C. diff (\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.mayoclinic.org\u002Fdiseases-conditions\u002Fc-difficile\u002Fbasics\u002Fdefinition\u002Fcon-20029664\"\u003EClostridium difficile\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, a bacterial infection), and spinal fluid in my brain. It was to the point where they basically told my family,&#xA0;&#x201C;Say your goodbyes.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EI recovered, obviously, and went to rehabilitation. I learned how to walk again with all of these people who just had their hips redone.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EIn the past year, the disease has started attacking my respiratory muscles. My diaphragm functions at about 18 percent, so breathing has become a difficulty. I carry around oxygen because if I talk for a long period of time, or walk for too long, I don&#x2019;t have the capacity to get my diaphragm moving and expand my lungs. This disease truly damages every inch of you.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EStrong Support\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EI&#x2019;m grateful that my entire family lives nearby. My number one supporter is my husband of four years.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EWe were high school sweethearts. I was a competitive gymnast and had a scholarship to be a vocal performance major. We were going to go to college together. We had goals. Then things changed, and he has been so adaptive and so supportive. Every hospital stay, he slept in that uncomfortable chair. I&#x2019;m in a hospital sometimes for thirty days.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E \n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"360\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F910a1647aa359f8b09d4875df0c50b8d074f42a2.jpg\"\u003E \n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cb\u003EChanel White with her husband, Noel White, who she calls her number one supporter. \u003C\u002Fb\u003E(Photo: Chelsey Shaw Photography)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EI absolutely would not be able to face this battle without him. I&#x2019;m not going to lie and say I don&#x2019;t have breakdowns and I don&#x2019;t get upset that I&#x2019;m dying at the age of 23. There are times when I can&#x2019;t be strong; it&#x2019;s just not in my power at that moment. He is able to look at me and just say, &#x201C;It&#x2019;s okay.&#x201D; Not that it&#x2019;s going to be okay because we both know that it&#x2019;s not going to be okay. But it is okay where we are at. We are together and he&#x2019;s going to be there.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ELearning to Let Go\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThis illness has opened my eyes to the world. Before I became ill, I really didn&#x2019;t have that perspective that life can be over in an instant. I never really had any major tragedies growing up. I never saw a lot of deaths. I never saw a lot of illness. And now I&#x2019;m thrust into this world where there is constant death and constant illness. I&#x2019;ve watched friends die. I&#x2019;ve watched just people go through suffering that no human should ever have to endure. I realize now that life is such a fragile thing and it can shatter in an instant. Once it does, you won&#x2019;t be able to put it back together &#x2014; you just have to move on as a changed person. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EI feel that I am a completely different individual since I became sick, like it opened this part of me that I just didn&#x2019;t know really existed. I&#x2019;m stronger, more resilient. I understand that I need to stop and take time to do the clich&#xE9;s, like smell the flowers, take the longer journey, and just enjoy the little things. Small victories are important. I am happy if I can have a bed. I am happy if I make it to the couch. I am happy if I am able to drink a small amount of Gatorade and not throw up.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EPeople might say that I learned not to take things for granted, but it&#x2019;s not like that. I don&#x2019;t think people are taking things for granted if they don&#x2019;t understand. I don&#x2019;t think someone is a bad person for eating a cheeseburger and not enjoying it. When you&#x2019;re sick, it&#x2019;s a different way of life. You learn to accept it. You learn that, wow, being able to eat a cheeseburger is really great. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EIt&#x2019;s not about whether you take things for granted or not. It&#x2019;s about understanding and accepting the life that you have. And making it the best you can. And celebrating what it is.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EChanel White blogs at&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fthetubefedwife.blogspot.com\u002F\"\u003Ethetubefedwife.blogspot.com\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERead This Next:\u003C\u002Fb\u003E \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002F6-phrases-people-facing-serious-illnesses-would-119951034923.html\"\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003E6 Phrases People Facing Serious Illnesses Would Rather Hear You Say\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003ELet&#x2019;s keep in touch! Gross Side Effect, And What You Can Do To Prevent It","summary":"Heres how to settle your stomach and still get the nutritional benefits.","body":"\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002Fc8a2067906ec160be69f2d39d8016252b856e902.jpg\" alt=\"Kale&#x2019;s Gross Side Effect, And What You Can Do To Prevent It\" width=\"540\" height=\"342\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cb\u003EKale giving you the runs? Here&#x2019;s how to settle your stomach and still get the nutritional benefits \u003C\u002Fb\u003E(Image from Thinkstock)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EYou already know that kale may be \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.menshealth.com\u002Fnutrition\u002Feasy-kale-recipes?cm_mmc=Yahoo-_-Kales_Gross_Side_Effects-_-Entry-_-Kale_Ultimate_Health_Food\"\u003EThe Ultimate Health Food\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. It&#x2019;s rich in vitamins A and C, potassium, calcium, iron, and folate, as well as the eye-healthy carotenoids lutein and zeaxanthin. It contains the flavonol kaempferol, which a study by Baylor College of Medicine researchers found helps stop pancreatic cancer cells from growing.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIt&#x2019;s one of the best things you can put in your body. But for some people, it exits the body in a less-than-pleasing way.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ELike how? Well, you may remember an unfortunate news item from 2013&#x2019;s Fashion Week in New York, when several models had to be &#x201C;treated &#x2026; for diarrhea from eating too much kale,&#x201D; according to the \u003Ci\u003ENew York Times\u003C\u002Fi\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThere&#x2019;s a simple reason for this superfood&#x2019;s supergross side effect: carbohydrates.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EKale is loaded with insoluble fiber and a carb called raffinose, neither of which can be broken down during digestion, explains Linda Ann Lee, M.D., director of the Johns Hopkins Integrative Medicine and Digestive Center.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EInstead, they both pass straight through your GI tract to your colon, where bacteria begin converting them to acids, gases, and alcohols.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe end result of this fermentation process: You&#x2019;re perched on the porcelain throne.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated:\u003C\u002Fb\u003E \u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.menshealth.com\u002Fnutrition\u002Fsnacks-you-can-actually-binge-eat?cm_mmc=Yahoo-_-Kales_Gross_Side_Effects-_-Entry-_-Foods_You_Can_Binge\"\u003E4 Foods You Can Actually Binge On\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAnother reason might be the volume of kale you&#x2019;re eating, especially if you&#x2019;re a kale newbie. &#x201C;Suddenly eating huge amounts of any high fiber food may cause digestive disturbances,&#x201D; &#xA0;says Colleen Gerg, R.D., a dietitian based in Philadelphia.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIt&#x2019;s easy to get carried away with kale consumption, especially if you&#x2019;re juicing it. &#x201C;Because juicing greens requires very large amounts of the vegetable to create a glass of juice, you&#x2019;re getting very high concentrations of nutrients which your body may not be used to in such large amounts,&#x201D; she says.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EGerg suggests mixing up your ingredients by &#x201C;eating the rainbow.&#x201D; Balance out the kale with some reds (red bell peppers, tomatoes, raspberries); blues and purples (blueberries, red\u002Fpurple cabbage); and orange and yellows (summer squash, butternut squash, cantaloupe).\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated:\u003Ci\u003E \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.menshealth.com\u002Fnutrition\u002Fhealthy-protein-smoothie-recipes?cm_mmc=Yahoo-_-Kales_Gross_Side_Effects-_-Entry-_-Protein_Packed_Smoothies\"\u003E20 Healthy, Protein-Packed Smoothie Recipes\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EGerg also recommends switching over to Tuscan kale, which has blue-green leaves and is less fibrous than red and curly Russian kale.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;It has a slightly sweeter, more earthy flavor,&#x201D; she says. &#x201C;Due to it&#x2019;s texture, it tends to be a bit more malleable and preferred when eating kale raw, as in salads.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EYou may also need to cut back to about half an ounce a few times a week.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EOn your kale-free days, Gerg suggests swapping in other good-for-you greens, such as Swiss chard, spinach, collard greens, mustard greens, or dark green lettuces like arugula, romaine lettuce, mache, and spring mix. They contain the same prized vitamins and minerals as kale, but less fiber.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EBy the Editors of Men&#x2019;s
